أسلم وإلا فرق بينهما وإباؤه طلاق لا إباؤها ولو أسلم أحدهما ثم لم تبن حتى تحيض مراده هنا أطلق في الآخر فشمل البالغ والصبي لكن بشرط التمييز حتى يفرق بينهما بإباء الصبي المميز باتفاق على الأصح، والفرق لأبي يوسف بين ردته وإبائه أن الإباء تمسك بما هو عليه فيكون صحيحاً، فأما الردة فإنشاء لما لم يكن موجوداً وهو يضره فلا يصح منه . كذا في المبسوط. وفيه : الأصل أن كل من صح منه الإسلام إذا أتى به يصح منه الإباء إذا عرض عليه ا هـ . وأما الصبي الذي لا يميز فإنه ينتظر عقله أي تمييزه والصبية كالصبي بخلاف ما إذ كان مجنوناً فإنه لا ينتظر بل يعرض على أبوية لأنه ليس له نهاية معلومة كالمرأة إذا وجدت الزوج عنيناً فإنه يؤجل، ولو مجبوباً فإنه لا يؤجل بل يفرق للحال لعدم الفائدة في الانتظار بخلاف العنين يؤجل لإفادته ومعنى العرض على أبوي المجنون أن أي الأبوين أسلم بقي النكاح لأنه يتبع المسلم منهما. كذا في فتح القدير. ويرد على المصنف ما إذا أسلم الزوج وهي مجوسية فتهودت أو تنصرت داما على النكاح كما لو كانت يهودية أو نصرانية من الابتداء. كذا في المبسوط . وقوله فإن أسلم وإلا فرق بينهما ينافيه . وقيد بالإسلام لأن النصرانية إذا تهودت أو عكسه لا يلتفت إليهم لأن الكفر كله ملة واحدة، وكذا لو تمجست زوجة النصراني فهما على نكاحهما كما لو كانت مجوسية في الابتداء ومعنى قوله «وإلا فرق بينهما أنه إن لم يسلم الآخر بأن أبى عنه فرق بينهما، وأما إذا لم يسلم ولم يمتنع . بأن سكت فإنه يكرر العرض عليه لما في الذخيرة إذا صرح بالإباء فالقاضي لا يعرض الإسلام عليه مرة أخرى ويفرق بينهما، فإن سكت ولم يقل شيئاً فالقاضي يعرض عليه الإسلام مرة بعد أخرى حتى تتم الثلاث احتياطاً ا هـ .
قوله: (وإباؤه طلاق لا إباؤها) وقال أبو يوسف : لا يكون طلاقاً في الوجهين لأن الفرقة بسبب يشترك فيها الزوجان فلا يكون طلاقاً كالفرقة بسبب الملك. ولهما أنه بالإباء امتنع عن الإمساك بالمعروف مع قدرته عليه بالإسلام فينوب القاضي منابه في التسريح بالإحسان كما في الجب والعنة أما المرأة فليست بأهل للطلاق فلا ينوب منابها عند إبائها . في الهداية ومراده أنه لا ينوب منابها في الطلاق لأنه ليس إليها وإنما ينوب منابها فيما إليها وهو التفريق على أنه فسخ والحاصل أنه نائب عن كل منهما فيما إليه لا كما يتوهم من عبارة الهداية أنه نائب عن الزوج لا عنها لأنه لو كان كذلك لم تتوقف الفرقة على القضاء فيما إذا كانت الآبية وليس مراده أن الطلاق يقع بمجرد إبائه كما هو ظاهر العبارة لما قدمه من
كذا
.
قوله : (ويرد على المصنف ما إذا أسلم الزوج الخ) قال الرملي قال في النهر : ويمكن أن يراد بالكتابية ولو مآلاً فلا . یرد اهـ. يعني في قوله الآتي ولم أسلم زوج الكتابية بقي نكاحها». أقول: وأحسن هذا أن المراد في كلامه بالزوجين الممتنع نكاحهما بعد إسلام أحدهما وبقيا على تلك الصفة وإلا كان يرد عليه أيضاً زوج الكتابية إذا أسلم وكان كتابياً أو مجوسياً تأمل قوله: (والحاصل أنه نائب عن
من
بقوله «فرق بينهما أي فرق القاضي بينهما، ولو وقع بمجرد إبائه لم يحتج إلى تفريق القاضي ولذا قالوا: وما لم يفرق القاضي بينهما فهي امرأته حتى يجب كمال المهر لها بموته قبل الدخول. وإنما لا يتوارثان لو مات أحدهما قبل التفريق للمانع منه وهو كفر أحدهما لا للبينونة، وسيأتي حكم المهر في الارتداد حيث قال : والإباء نظيره وأطلق في الزوج فشمل الصغير والكبير والمجنون فيكون إباء الصبي المميز طلاقاً على الأصح كما في المبسوط، وإباء أحد أبوي المجنون طلاقاً أيضاً مع أن الطلاق لا منهما لما ذكرنا من المعنى قالوا: وهي يصح من أغرب المسائل حيث يقع الطلاق منهما نظيره إذا كانا مجبوبين أو كان المجنون عنيناً فإن القاضي يفرق بينهما ويكون طلاقاً اتفاقاً وتحقيقه أن الصبي والمجنون أهلان للوقوع لا للإيقاع بدليل أن الصبي إذا ورث قريبه فإنه يعتق عليه. وما نحن فيه وقوع لا إيقاع، ونظيره كل منهما فيما إليه) قال الرملي : وهو الطلاق منه والفسخ منها قوله : (وإباء أحد أبوي المجنون) المراد تعميم الأبي سواء كان الأب أو الأم أي إذا وجد أحدهما وأبي يكون طلاقاً فلا . یرد أنه لو وجد أو أبي أحدهما وأسلم الآخر يصير مسلماً تبعاً لأشرفهما ديناً. وفي التحرير وشرحه قوله: (وصح إسلامه) أي المجنون تبعاً لأبويه أو أحدهما كالصبي (وإنما يعرض الإسلام لإسلام زوجته على أبيه أو أمه لصيرورته مسلماً بإسلامه أي إسلام أحدهما فإن أسلم أقرا على النكاح، وإن أبى فرق بينهما دفعاً للضرر عن المسلمة بالقدر الممكن قوله : (وإنما عرض على وليه إذا أسلمت زوجته قوله : (دفعاً للضرر عنها إذ ليس له أي الجنون (نهاية معلومة) ففي التأخير ضرر بها مع ما فيه من الفساد لقدرة المجنون على الوطء ثم قال شمس الأئمة : ليس المراد من عرض الإسلام على والده أن يعرض عليه بطريق الإلزام بل على سبيل الشفقة المعلومة من الآباء على الأولاد عادة فلعل ذلك يحمله على أن يسلم، ألا ترى أنه إذا لم يكن له والدان جعل القاضي له خصماً وفرق بينهما، فهذا دليل على أن الأباء يسقط اعتباره هنا للتعذر قوله : ( ويصير مرتداً تبعاً بارتداد أبويه ولحاقهما به أي بالمجنون بدار الحرب قوله : (إذا بلغ مجنوناً وهما (مسلمان) لأنه قد ثبت الإسلام في حقه تبعاً لهما فيزول بزوال ما يتبعه، ثم كون أبويه مسلمين ليس بقيد لأن إسلام أحدهما وارتداد لحوقه معه بدار الحرب كافٍ في ارتداده قوله : (بخلاف ما إذا تركاه في دار الإسلام) فإنه يكون مسلماً لظهور تبعية الدار بزوال تبعية الأبوين لأنها كالخلف عنهما قوله : (أو بلغ مسلماً ثم جن أو أسلم عاقلاً فجن) قبل البلوغ قوله : فارتدا ولحقا به بدار الحرب لأنه صار أصلاً في الإيمان يتقرر ركنه فلا ينعدم بالتبعية أو عروض الجنون ا هـ قوله : ( ونظيره إذا كانا مجبوبين) من الجب وهو قطع الذكر، وضمير «كانا» يرجع الصبي المميز والكبير المجنون. وقوله أو كان المجنون عنينا قيد به لأن الصغير العنين ينتظر بلوغه قوله : (وما نحن فيه وقوع لا إيقاع جواب عن الاستغراب ونظر فيه بعض الفضلاء لتصريحهم بأنه إنما كان إباؤه طلاقاً لأنه لما مات الإمساك بالمعروف وجب التسريح بالإحسان، فإن فعل وإلا ناب القاضي منابه فكان تفريق القاضي بإبائه بطريق النيابة عن المميز وأحد أبوي المجنون وفعل النائب إلى
If one converts and the other refuses, the judge separates them. His refusal is a divorce, not her refusal. Even if one of them converts, she does not become separated until she menstruates. Here the author generalizes the other spouse to include adult and child, but with the condition of discernment, so separation occurs by the refusal of the discerning child by agreement on the sound view. The difference for Abu Yusuf between his apostasy and his refusal is that refusal is adherence to what he is upon, so it is valid; as for apostasy, it is initiating something nonexistent, which harms him, so it is not valid from him. So in al-Mabsut. In it: The principle is that whoever's Islam is valid, his refusal is valid when presented to him. As for the nondiscerning child, he is awaited for his intellect, i.e., discernment. The girl is like the boy. Unlike if he is insane, then he is not awaited; rather it is presented to his parents because he has no known end, like a woman when she finds her husband impotent: he is given a reprieve, but if he is castrated (majbub), no reprieve is given; separation is immediate due to lack of benefit in waiting, unlike the impotent who is given a reprieve for its benefit. The meaning of presenting to the parents of the insane is that whichever parent converts, the marriage remains because he follows the one with the better religion. So in Fath al-Qadir. An objection is raised against the author regarding when the husband converts while the wife is Magian then she becomes Jewish or Christian: they remain in marriage, as if she were Jewish or Christian from the beginning. So in al-Mabsut. And his statement 'if he converts, otherwise separate them' contradicts it. He restricted to Islam because if a Christian woman becomes Jewish or vice versa, no attention is paid to them because all disbelief is one religion. Likewise, if the wife of a Christian becomes Magian, they remain in marriage as if she were Magian from the beginning. The meaning of his statement 'otherwise separate them' is that if the other does not convert by refusing, the judge separates them. If he neither converts nor refuses by remaining silent, the presentation is repeated. According to al-Dhakhira: if he explicitly refuses, the judge does not present Islam to him again and separates them; if he remains silent and says nothing, the judge presents Islam to him again and again up to three times as a precaution.
His statement: (And his refusal is a divorce, not her refusal). Abu Yusuf said: It is not a divorce in either case because the separation is due to a cause in which both spouses participate, so it is not a divorce like separation due to ownership (milkiyyat). Their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) argument: By refusing, he refrains from retaining (his wife) in a recognized manner despite being able to do so by converting, so the judge acts as his deputy in releasing with kindness, as in the case of a castrated or impotent man. As for the woman, she is not qualified for divorce, so the judge does not act as her deputy upon her refusal. In al-Hidayah: His intent is that he does not act as her deputy in divorce because it is not her prerogative; rather he acts as her deputy in what is her prerogative, which is dissolution (faskh). The conclusion is that he is a deputy for each of them in what pertains to them, not as might be misunderstood from al-Hidayah's phrasing that he is a deputy for the husband, not her, because if so, the separation would not depend on the judge's ruling when the woman refuses. He does not mean that the divorce occurs by his mere refusal, as the apparent wording suggests, due to what he mentioned.
His statement: (An objection is raised against the author regarding when the husband converts, etc.) al-Ramli said: In al-Nahr: Possibly he meant by 'kitabiyyah' even eventually, so no objection. Meaning in his future statement 'and if the husband of a kitabiyyah converts, her marriage remains'. I say: The best of this is that he means in his speech the spouses whose marriage is prevented after one's conversion and they remain in that state; otherwise it would also be objected against him regarding the husband of a kitabiyyah if he converts while he was a kitabi or Magian. Consider.
His statement: (And the conclusion is that he is a deputy for) through his statement 'separate them' i.e., the judge separates them. If it occurred by his mere refusal, there would be no need for the judge's separation. Therefore they said: As long as the judge has not separated them, she is his wife, so full dower is obligatory upon his death before consummation. They do not inherit from each other if one dies before separation due to the impediment of one's disbelief, not due to separation. The ruling of dower in apostasy will come where he said: Refusal is analogous to it. He generalised the husband to include minor, adult, and insane, so the refusal of a discerning minor is a divorce on the sound view as in al-Mabsut. Also the refusal of one of the insane person's parents is a divorce, even though divorce is not from them, due to the meaning we mentioned. They said: This is one of the strangest issues where divorce occurs from them. Its analogy is if both are castrated or if the insane is impotent, then the judge separates them and it is a divorce by agreement. Its verification is that the minor and insane are qualified for occurrence (wuqu') not for initiation (iqa'). Evidence: if a minor inherits his relative, he emancipates a slave. Our case is occurrence, not initiation. Its analogy is each of them in what pertains to them. al-Ramli said: Divorce from him and faskh from her. His statement: (The refusal of one of the insane person's parents) means generalising the parent whether father or mother: i.e., if one of them is present and refuses, it is a divorce. So it is not objected that if one of them is found and refuses while the other converts, he becomes Muslim by following the better religion. In al-Tahrir and its commentary: His statement: (And his Islam is valid) i.e., the insane person's Islam valid by following his parents or one of them, like the minor. (Presentation of Islam to his father or mother is for the sake of his wife's Islam so that he becomes Muslim by their Islam. If either converts, they are confirmed in marriage. If he refuses, they are separated to avoid harm to the Muslim woman as much as possible. His statement: (It is presented to his guardian when his wife converts). His statement: (To avoid harm to her, since he, i.e., the insane, has no known end), so delay harms her along with the corruption due to the insane's ability to have intercourse. Then Shams al-A'imma said: Presenting Islam to his father is not by way of compulsion but out of the known compassion of fathers for their children, hoping it will make him convert. Do you not see that if he has no parents, the judge appoints an opponent for him and separates them? This indicates that the refusal is disregarded here due to impossibility. His statement: (And he becomes an apostate by following the apostasy of his parents and their joining him, i.e., the insane, in dar al-harb). His statement: (If he reaches puberty insane while both are Muslim) because Islam has been established for him through following them, so it is removed by the removal of what he followed. Then the fact that both parents are Muslim is not a condition because one parent's Islam and apostasy by joining him in dar al-harb suffices for his apostasy. His statement: (Unlike if they leave him in dar al-Islam) then he remains Muslim due to the dominance of following the abode over following the parents, as it stands in for them. His statement: (Or if he reaches puberty Muslim then becomes insane, or converts while sane then becomes insane) before puberty. His statement: (Then they apostatize and join him in dar al-harb) because he has become an original in faith; its pillar is established, so it is not nullified by following or by the occurrence of insanity. His statement: (And its analogy is if both are castrated) i.e., al-jabb meaning cutting off the penis. The pronoun 'they' refers to the discerning minor and the adult insane. His statement 'or if the insane is impotent' is a qualification because the child who is impotent is awaited till puberty. His statement: (And our case is occurrence, not initiation) is a response to the astonishment. Some scholars have examined it because they explicitly said that his refusal is a divorce because when retaining with kindness is impossible, releasing with kindness becomes obligatory. If he does so, otherwise the judge acts as his deputy. So the judge's separation by his refusal is by way of deputyship for the discerning minor and one parent of the insane, and the action of the deputy extends to...

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq on Kanz al-Daqaiq, addressing the ruling when one spouse converts to Islam and the other refuses. The author begins by stating the basic rule: if one spouse converts and the other refuses, the judge separates them. The husband's refusal is considered a divorce (talaq), while the wife's refusal is not a divorce but a judicial dissolution (faskh). The commentary clarifies that this applies to both adults and children, provided the child has discernment (tamyiz). For a nondiscerning child, the judge awaits his maturation. For an insane spouse, the judge presents Islam to his parents, and if either parent converts, the marriage remains because the insane follows the parent with the better religion. The passage then addresses an objection: if the husband converts while his wife is a Magian and she subsequently becomes Jewish or Christian, the marriage continues. This is because all non-Islamic religions are considered one millah, so a change within disbelief is ignored. The commentary then discusses the dispute with Abu Yusuf regarding the nature of the husband's refusal. Abu Yusuf holds that the refusal does not constitute a divorce because the separation is due to a cause shared by both spouses, similar to separation by ownership (e.g., a slave marriage). Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the husband, by refusing, fails to retain his wife in a recognized manner despite being able to convert; thus the judge acts as his deputy in effecting a divorce, analogous to cases of impotence ('innah) or castration (jabb). The wife, not being eligible to divorce, does not have the judge act as her deputy; hence her refusal results in a faskh, not a talaq. The commentary emphasizes that the judge acts as a deputy for each spouse in what pertains to them. The passage also covers the insane spouse in detail: his refusal to Islam, through his parents, is considered a talaq, even though he is not legally capable of divorce. This is because the ruling is on the 'occurrence' (wuqu') of divorce, not the 'initiation' (iqa')—the divorce is attributed to the judge's action. Similarly, the minor with discernment's refusal is a divorce. The commentary further discusses apostasy of the insane by following his parents' apostasy and joining dar al-harb, contrasting it with being left in dar al-Islam. It also draws analogies to cases of castration and impotence, where the judge's separation is considered a talaq by agreement.

Key Terms
إباء (iba'): Refusal to embrace Islam after being offered it following the spouse's conversion.
نيابة (niyabah): Deputyship; the judge acts as deputy for the spouse in effecting separation.
فرقة (furqah): Separation between spouses due to difference in religion after conversion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the legal classification of the judge's separation when the husband refuses Islam after his wife converts?
A) A judicial dissolution (faskh) for both spouses
B) A divorce (talaq) from the husband
C) A dissolution due to apostasy (riddah)
D) An automatic annulment of the marriage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the husband's refusal of Islam after his spouse's conversion results in a judge-issued talaq (divorce), while the wife's refusal results in a faskh (judicial dissolution).

Nikah — Marriage
advanced
10 min
Court-Ordered Divorce upon Refusal to Convert: Talaq or Faskh?
Explaining rulings on marriage dissolution due to conversion or apostasy, including guardian's refusal and court intervention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the judge's separation upon refusal to convert as a talaq from the husband, and state the legal consequences regarding 'idda, mahr, and inheritance.

Core Idea
The Hanafi court-ordered separation for refusal to convert is a divorce from the husband, not an annulment, based on istihsan and the principle of deputyship.

When a spouse converts to Islam and the other refuses, the judge must separate them. A critical question arises: is this separation a divorce (talaq) or an annulment (faskh)? The Hanafi school, using istihsan and analogical reasoning, holds that it is a talaq from the husband, even if he is a minor or insane. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Determine when judicial separation becomes necessary: upon one spouse's refusal to convert after the other's conversion. Note that mere refusal does not dissolve the marriage; the judge's action is required.
The marriage continues until the judge separates them.
2
Distinguish wuqu' and iqa'
Understand the difference between occurrence (wuqu') and issuance (iqa'). A minor or insane person can be the subject of a legal effect (wuqu') but cannot initiate it (iqa'). This is key to why divorce can occur from them legally.
The passage uses the analogy of a minor inheriting and causing emancipation.
3
Apply the analogy of inheritance
Just as a minor who inherits a relative can have emancipation occur on him (the slave is freed), similarly divorce can occur on a minor/insane through the judge's action.
The 'illa is the capacity to be an object of legal effects.
4
Understand the judge's role as deputy
The judge acts as a deputy (na'ib) on behalf of the husband. The deputy's action is attributed to the principal, so the divorce is legally from the husband.
This deputyship is based on necessity: the need to protect the Muslim wife from harm.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if it is talaq, the wife observes 'idda and can be taken back during 'idda if revocable; if it is faskh, no 'idda and immediate dissolution.
Hanafi school relies on the position that it is talaq.

يفرق بينهما ويكون طلاقاً اتفاقاً وتحقيقه أن الصبي والمجنون أهلان للوقوع لا للإيقاع بدليل أن الصبي إذا ورث قريبه فإنه يعتق عليه. وما نحن فيه وقوع لا إيقاع، ونظيره كل منهما فيما إليه) قال الرملي : وهو لأشرفهما ديناً. وفي التحرير وشرحه قوله: (وصح إسلامه) أي المجنون تبعاً لأبويه أو أحدهما كالصبي (وإنما يعرض الإسلام لإسلام زوجته على أبيه أو أمه لصيرورته مسلماً بإسلامه أي إسلام أحدهما فإن أسلم أقرا على الفساد لقدرة المجنون على الوطء ثم قال شمس الأئمة : ليس المراد من عرض الإسلام على والده أن يعرض عليه بطريق الإلزام بل على سبيل الشفقة المعلومة من الآباء على الأولاد عادة فلعل ذلك يحمله على أن يسلم، ألا بلغ مجنوناً وهما (مسلمان) لأنه قد ثبت الإسلام في حقه تبعاً لهما فيزول بزوال ما يتبعه، ثم كون أبويه مسلمين ليس بقيد لأن إسلام أحدهما وارتداد لحوقه معه بدار الحرب كافٍ في ارتداده قوله : (بخلاف ما إذا أصلاً في الإيمان يتقرر ركنه فلا ينعدم بالتبعية أو عروض الجنون ا هـ قوله : ( ونظيره إذا كانا مجبوبين) من الجب وهو قطع الذكر، وضمير «كانا» يرجع الصبي المميز والكبير المجنون. وقوله أو كان المجنون عنينا قيد به لأن الصغير العنين ينتظر بلوغه قوله : (وما نحن فيه وقوع لا إيقاع جواب عن الاستغراب ونظر فيه بعض الفضلاء لتصريحهم بأنه إنما كان إباؤه طلاقاً لأنه لما مات الإمساك بالمعروف وجب التسريح بالإحسان، فإن فعل وإلا ناب القاضي منابه فكان تفريق القاضي بإبائه بطريق النيابة عن المميز وأحد أبوي المجنون وفعل النائب منسوب للمنوب عنه لا محاله فكان الطلاق واقعاً منهما حكماً ا.هـ. قلت : ويؤيده أن شمس الأئمة (مسلمة الأولى إسقاط الواوقوله : (بخلاف ما إذا كانت كافرة وأسلم الزوج فلا نفقة لها قال في الشرنبلالية شامل للصغيرة المجنونة التي فرق بإباء والدها قبل الدخول بها ولا نفع لها في إسقاط حقها فيكون وارداً على أنه لا يتصرف إلا فيما فيه نفع للصغير فلينظر جوابه قوله : (وظاهره أنه لا فرق الخ هذا الظاهر خلاف الظاهر بل الظاهر أنه خاص بما إذا كان هو الآبي ليكون إباؤه طلاقاً كما هو مقتضى التشبيه في قوله كما لو وقعت الفرقة بالخلع أو بالجب والعنة فإنها فرقة من جانبه فتكون طلاقاً ومعتدة الطلاق يقع عليها الطلاق، أما لو كان الآبي تكون الفرقة فسخاً لأنها ليست أهلاً للطلاق والفسخ رفع ا للعقد فلا يقع الطلاق في عدته . والظاهر أن هذا وجه ما في الفتح لكن سيأتي أول كتاب الطلاق أنه لا يقع طلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وفي ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً قوله : (ليس سبباً) بل هي

لو علق الزوج الطلاق بشرط وهو عاقل فجن ثم وجد الشرط وقع عليه وهو مجنون لما ذكرنا . وأشار بالطلاق إلى وجوب العدة عليها إن كان دخل بها لأن المرأة إذا كانت مسلمة فقد التزمت أحكام الإسلام ومن حكمه وجوب العدة، وإن كانت كافرة لا تعتقد وجوبها لأن الزوج مسلم والعدة حقه وحقوقنا لا تبطل بديانتهم. وأشار أيضاً إلى وجوب النفقة لها ما دامت في العدة وإن كانت المرأة مسلمة لأن المنع من الاستمتاع جاء من جهة الزوج وهو غير مسقط بخلاف ما إذا كانت كافرة وأسلم الزوج فلا نفقة لها لأن المنع من جهتها ولذا لا مهر لها إن كان قبل الدخول. وأشار أيضاً إلى وقوع طلاقه عليها ما دامت في العدة كما لو وقعت الفرقة بالخلع أو بالجب والعنة كذا في المحيط وظاهره أنه لا فرق في وقوع الطلاق أن يكون هو الآبي أوهي، وظاهر ما في فتح القدير أنه خاص بما إذا كان هو الآبي ليكون إباؤه طلاقاً كما هو مقتضى التشبيه في قوله كما لو وقعت الفرقة بالخلع أو بالجب والعنة فإنها فرقة من جانبه فتكون طلاقاً ومعتدة الطلاق يقع عليها الطلاق، أما لو كان الآبي تكون الفرقة فسخاً لأنها ليست أهلاً للطلاق والفسخ رفع ا للعقد فلا يقع الطلاق في عدته . والظاهر أن هذا وجه ما في الفتح لكن سيأتي أول كتاب الطلاق أنه لا يقع طلاق في عدة عن فسخ إلا في تفريق القاضي بإباء أحدهما عن الإسلام وفي ارتداد أحدهما مطلقاً قوله : (ليس سبباً) بل هي

قوله: (ولو أسلم أحدهما ثمة لم تبن حتى تحيض ثلاثاً فإذا حاضت ثلاثاً بانت) لأن الإسلام ليس سبباً للفرقة والعرض على الإسلام متعذر لقصور الولاية ولا بد من الفرقة دفعاً للفساد فأقمنا شرطها وهو مضي الحيض مقام السبب كما في حفر البئر. أطلقه فشمل المدخول بها وغيرها، وهذا دليل على أن هذه الحيض ليس بعدة لأنها لو كانت عدة لاختصت بالمدخول بها، ولم يذكر المصنف عليها بعد ذلك عدة لعدم وجوبها لأن المرأة إن كانت حربية فلا عدة عليها، وإن كانت المسلمة فكذلك عند أبي حنيفة خلافاً لهما كما سيأتي في هي الأئمة
Book of Marriage, Section on Marriage of the Disbeliever. By his statement 'He separated between them' i.e., the judge separated between them, and if it had occurred by his mere refusal, there would be no need for the judge's separation. Therefore they said: As long as the judge has not separated them, she is his wife, so that the full mahr becomes obligatory for her by his death before consummation. They do not inherit from each other if one dies before separation due to the impediment which is the disbelief of one, not due to separation. The ruling of mahr in apostasy will come later where he said: And refusal is its counterpart. He generalized regarding the husband, covering the minor, the adult, and the insane. Thus, the refusal of a discerning minor is divorce according to the most correct view as in al-Mabsut. The refusal of one parent of the insane is also divorce, although divorce does not come from them for the meaning we mentioned. They said: This is among the strangest issues where divorce occurs from them. Its analogy is when they are both castrated or if the insane one is impotent, then the judge separates between them and it is divorce by agreement. Its verification is that the minor and the insane are capable of occurrence (wuqu') not of issuance (iqa'). Evidence: if a minor inherits from his relative, he emancipates a slave. Our case is occurrence, not issuance. Its analogy is each of them in what pertains to them. Al-Ramli said: It is divorce from him and annulment (faskh) from her. His statement: (And the refusal of one parent of the insane) means generalizing the refusal whether father or mother; i.e., if one of them is present and refuses, it is divorce, so it is not objected that if he is present and one refuses and the other becomes Muslim, he becomes Muslim following the more honorable in religion. In al-Tahrir and its commentary: His statement: (And his Islam is valid) i.e., the insane follows his parents or one of them like the minor. (And he presents Islam for the Islam of his wife to his father or mother because he becomes Muslim by his Islam i.e., the Islam of one of them. If he becomes Muslim, they are confirmed in marriage; if he refuses, separation is made between them to protect the Muslim woman as much as possible.) His statement: (And he presents it to his guardian if his wife becomes Muslim.) His statement: (To protect her from harm since he i.e., the insane has no known end.) Thus delay causes harm to her along with the corruption due to the insane's ability to have intercourse. Then Shams al-A'imma said: The meaning of presenting Islam to his father is not to present it obligatorily, but out of the compassion known from fathers towards children normally; perhaps that will motivate him to become Muslim. Do you not see that if he has no parents, the judge appoints an adversary for him and separates them? This indicates that the father's consideration drops here due to impossibility. His statement: (And he becomes an apostate by following the apostasy of his parents and their joining him) i.e., the insane in Dar al-Harb. His statement: (If he reaches puberty insane while they are Muslims) because Islam was established for him by following them, so it ceases with the cessation of what is followed. Then the fact that his parents are Muslims is not a precondition because the Islam of one of them and apostasy and joining him in Dar al-Harb is sufficient for his apostasy. His statement: (Contrary to if they leave him in Dar al-Islam) because he remains Muslim due to the dominance of the domicile's following over the parent's following, as it takes their place. His statement: (Or if he reaches puberty Muslim then becomes insane, or becomes Muslim sane then becomes insane) before puberty. His statement: Then they apostatized and joined him in Dar al-Harb because he became an original in faith, its pillar is established, so it does not cease by following or by the occurrence of insanity. End. His statement: (And its analogy is if they are both castrated) from al-jabb which is cutting the penis. The pronoun 'they' refers to the discerning minor and the adult insane. His statement: 'Or if the insane is impotent' restricts because the impotent minor waits for his puberty. His statement: (Our case is occurrence, not issuance) is a response to the objection. Some scholars examined it because they explicitly stated that his refusal is divorce because when retention with kindness ceased, release with goodness became obligatory. If he does it, fine; otherwise, the judge acts in his place. Thus the judge's separation due to his refusal is by way of deputyship on behalf of the discerning minor and one parent of the insane. The deputy's action is attributed to the principal necessarily, so divorce occurs from them legally. End. I say: It is supported by Shams al-A'imma's verification that divorce belongs to the ownership of marriage, as there is no harm in establishing the ownership itself but in issuance. So when the need arises for valid issuance of divorce from him to repel harm, it is valid. Its completion is in the chapter on impediments from Sharh al-Tahrir. His statement: (And if she is [Muslim]) the first is dropping the waw. His statement: (Contrary to if she is a disbeliever and the husband becomes Muslim, she has no maintenance.) He said in al-Shurnubulaliyya: Including the minor or insane woman who was separated by her father's refusal before consummation, and she has no benefit in dropping her right, so it is an objection that one does not act except in the child's interest. Let his answer be considered. His statement: (And apparently there is no difference...) This apparent is contrary to apparent; rather, it is specific to when he is the one refusing so that his refusal is divorce as required by the analogy in his statement: 'Just as if separation occurred by khul' or by castration or impotence, it is separation from his side, so it is divorce, and during the idda of divorce divorce occurs on her. But if she is the one refusing, the separation is annulment because she is not eligible for divorce, and annulment is a lifting of the contract, so divorce does not occur in its idda.' And it appears that this is the interpretation in al-Fath, but it will come at the beginning of the Book of Divorce that no divorce occurs in idda from annulment except in the judge's separation due to refusal regarding Islam and in apostasy of one of them absolutely. His statement: (It is not a cause) but rather it is...

His statement: (And if one of them becomes Muslim in that place, she does not separate until she menstruates three times; when she menstruates three times, she separates) because Islam is not a cause for separation, and presenting Islam is impossible due to lack of guardianship. Separation is necessary to prevent corruption, so we made its condition, which is the passage of menstruation, take the place of the cause, like digging a well. He generalized, covering the one with whom he had consummated and others. This indicates that these menstruations are not idda because if they were idda, they would be specific to the one with whom marriage was consummated. The author did not mention after that any idda because it is not obligatory. For if the woman is a harbiyah, she has no idda; and if she is Muslim, likewise according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) as will come in the section on (she) from the scholars.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discusses the rulings pertaining to marriage when one spouse converts to Islam or apostatizes. The passage type is an expansion probe, where the commentator (Ibn Nujaym) explains and justifies the rulings stated in the matn. The central issue is the legal effect of a spouse's conversion or apostasy on the marriage contract, and the role of the judge in effecting separation.

The author begins by clarifying that if a spouse converts to Islam and the other refuses, the judge must separate them; mere refusal does not itself dissolve the marriage. Until the judge separates, the marriage continues, so for example, if the non-Muslim husband dies before separation, the wife is entitled to the full mahr. This is because the impediment to inheritance is the disbelief of one party, not the separation itself. The discussion then focuses on the case where the refusing spouse is a minor or insane. The commentator explains that the refusal of a discerning minor (al-sabi al-mumayyiz) is considered a divorce (talaq) according to the most correct view, as recorded in al-Mabsut. Similarly, the refusal of one parent of an insane person is also considered a divorce. This seems strange because divorce normally issues from the husband himself, not from his guardian. The commentator resolves this by distinguishing between occurrence (wuqu') and issuance (iqa'). The minor and insane are capable of having divorce occur on them (wuqu'), but not of issuing it themselves (iqa'). An analogy is given: if a minor inherits a slave, he can become the owner and if a relative is to be emancipated due to the slave, it happens; similarly here, the divorce occurs from them legally because the judge acts as a deputy (na'ib) on their behalf. The deputy's action is attributed to the principal.

Further, the commentator discusses the case where both spouses are castrated (majbuban) or the insane husband is impotent ('anin). In such cases, the judge separates them by agreement (ittifaqan), and it is considered a divorce. The rationale is the same: the need to protect the Muslim woman from harm and the impossibility of normal marital life.

The passage then addresses the scenario where a Muslim woman is married to a non-Muslim man who converts later. If the husband converts, the marriage is confirmed; if he refuses, the judge separates them. The conversion of one parent of an insane or minor husband makes the child Muslim by following (taba'iyyah). If the parent apostatizes and joins Dar al-Harb, the child also becomes an apostate if left in Dar al-Harb, but if left in Dar al-Islam, the child remains Muslim due to the dominance of the domicile.

The commentator then moves to the ruling that if a husband conditionally divorces while sane, then becomes insane, and the condition is later fulfilled, the divorce occurs even during his insanity. This is based on the principle that the divorce is connected to the ownership of marriage, and the need to prevent harm.

Finally, the passage discusses the rule regarding conversion to Islam in a non-Muslim country (thammat). The separation does not occur immediately upon conversion; instead, the wife must wait for three menstrual cycles (hayd) to pass. If they pass without the other spouse converting, the marriage is dissolved. This interim period is not technically an 'idda (waiting period after divorce), because 'idda only applies after consummation, while this rule applies even before consummation. The commentator notes that this ruling is based on necessity: since presenting Islam is impossible, the passing of time substitutes for the cause of separation.

The commentator also addresses various subsidiary points: the obligation of maintenance (nafaqah) during the 'idda, whether the separation is considered talaq or faskh (annulment), and the differing views of Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding 'idda for a Muslim woman in this context.

Throughout, the reasoning is grounded in Hanafi usul: istihsan (juristic preference) and qiyas (analogy) are used to resolve novel cases. The authority weight of these rulings is primarily from the Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad), as indicated by references to al-Mabsut and the agreement of the earlier masters. The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the judge's separation is a divorce from the husband, not an annulment, except in specific cases where it is annulment, as will be detailed in the Book of Divorce.

Key Terms
إباء (iba'): Refusal of the non-Muslim spouse to convert to Islam upon the Muslim spouse's conversion.
تفريق القاضي (tafriq al-qadi): The judge's judicial separation between spouses due to a legal cause, such as one spouse's refusal to convert.
وقوع وإيقاع (wuqu' wa iqa'): Wuqu' (occurrence) is the effect of a legal action taking place on a person; iqa' (issuance) is the active initiation of a legal action. The text distinguishes that minor/insane can have divorce occur on them (wuqu') but cannot issue it (iqa').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the legal effect of a court-ordered separation when a husband (who is a minor or insane) refuses to convert to Islam?
A) It is an annulment (faskh) because the husband cannot issue divorce.
B) It is a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) that occurs from the husband legally, through the judge's deputyship.
C) The separation is invalid until the husband reaches puberty or recovers sanity.
D) The wife must observe 'idda only if consummation occurred, and no divorce pronouncements affect her.

Key Takeaway
The judge's separation upon refusal to convert is a talaq from the husband, not an annulment, because the judge acts as a deputy and the minor/insane are capable of wuqu'.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

Separation When One Spouse Converts in Dar al-Harb: Waiting Period and Legal Nature
Explains the waiting period and nature of separation when one spouse converts in enemy territory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the waiting period required for separation when one spouse converts in dar al-harb and distinguish between the Hanafi positions on whether the separation constitutes talaq or faskh.

Core Idea
Three menses after conversion trigger separation, not as 'idda but as a condition; its legal nature is disputed between talaq and faskh.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a complex scenario: when one spouse accepts Islam in enemy territory. Because Islamic authority is absent, a waiting period substitutes for a judge's decree. The author explains the conditions and then notes the internal Hanafi disagreement on whether this separation is a divorce or an annulment. Understanding this ruling clarifies the rules of marriage and conversion across jurisdictions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger and the waiting period
The conversion of one spouse in dar al-harb triggers a potential separation, but not immediately. The condition is the passage of three menses (or three months for non-menstruating women). Note that this waiting period is not a full 'idda.
The text explicitly distinguishes this period from 'idda.
2
Understand the legal rationale
Separation is necessary to prevent corruption, but the judge cannot intervene due to lack of jurisdiction. So the passage of time is substituted for the judge's decree, analogous to the case of digging a well (where time substitutes for other causes).
Familiarize yourself with the concept of iqamat al-shart maqam al-sabab.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold the separation is talaq; Abu Yusuf holds it is faskh. Their arguments hinge on whether the substitute (time) takes the ruling of the original (judge's decree) or the absence of judicial intervention makes it akin to apostasy.
The mufta bihi is that it is talaq.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
If talaq, the husband can revoke during the waiting period, and divorces pronounced count. If faskh, no further repercussions. This practical difference affects subsequent marriage and inheritance.
Consider two scenarios: husband pronounces divorce during the three menses.
5
Note the scope and exceptions
The ruling applies only while the spouses remain separated by dar al-harb; if the other converts before the period ends, no separation. Also, if the husband is originally a Kitabi (for a Muslim woman? The passage ends with exclusion: if the husband of a Kitabiyya converts, marriage remains; if the wife becomes Majusiyya, separation occurs.
The text also mentions 32 aspects derived from permutations of locations.

قولهما. وأفاد بتوقف البينونة على الحيض أن الآخر لو أسلم قبل انقضائها فلا بينونة وأطلق في الإسلام أحدهما في دار الحرب فشمل ما إذا كان الآخر في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب أقام الآخر فيها أو خرج إلى دار الإسلام فحاصله أنه ما لم يجتمعا في دار الإسلام فإنه لا يعرض الإسلام على المصر، سواء خرج المسلم أو الآخر، لأنه لا يقضى لغائب ولا على غائب. كذا في المحيط. وأشار بالحيض إلى أنها من ذواته فلو كانت لا تحيض لصغر أو كبر فلا تبين إلا بمضي ثلاثة أشهر. وبهذا علم أن مسألة ما إذا أسلم أحد الزوجين على اثنين وثلاثين وجهاً لأن الثمانية المتقدمة على أربعة لأنهما إما أن يكونا في دار الإسلام أو في دار الحرب أو أحدهما في دار الإسلام فقط وهو صادق بصورتين. ولم يبين صفة البينونة هل هي طلاق أو فسخ للاختلاف ففي السير أنها طلاق عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن انصرام هذه المدة جعل بدلاً عن قضاء القاضي والبدل قائم مقام الأصل، وعند أبي يوسف فسخ وهو رواية عنهما لأن هذه فرقة وقعت حكماً لا بتفريق القاضي فكانت فسخاً بمنزلة ردة الزوج وملكه امرأته كذا في المحيط. وينبغي أن يقال : إن كان المسلم هي فهي فرقة بطلاق لأن الآبي هو الزوج حكماً وقد أقيم مضي المدة مقام إبائه وتفريق القاضي وإباؤه طلاق عندهما فكذا ما قام مقامه، وإن كان المسلم هو الزوج فهي فسخ لما تقدم في إبائها فكذا حكم ما قام مقامه . وأما وقوع الطلاق عليها فإن كان قبل البينونة فلا إشكال في الوقوع لأنها زوجة، وإن كان بعد البينونة بمضي المدة فإن كان في العدة عند من أوجبها وقع وإلا فلا. وأما عند من لم يوجبها فهي أجنبية من كل وجه فلا يقع شيء، ولا شك أن هذه أفراد المسألة السابقة ففيها الأقسام الستة، وأما القسمان الآخران فخارجان بقوله من قوله : (ولو أسلم زوج الكتابية بقي نكاحهما) فهو مخصص لكل من المسألتين صادق بصورتين ما إذا كان الزوج كتابياً أو مجوسياً لأنه يصح النكاح بينهما ابتداء فلأن يبقى أولى، ولو تمجست يفرق بينهما لفساد النكاح.
His saying: 'And if one of them converts to Islam there, she does not become separated until she menstruates three times; when she has menstruated three times she becomes separated.' Because Islam is not a cause for separation, and presenting Islam [to the other] is impossible due to lack of authority, and separation is necessary to prevent corruption, so we establish its condition, which is the passage of menstruation, in place of the cause, like digging a well. He made it absolute, so it includes the one who was consummated with and others, and this is evidence that these menses are not an 'iddah because if they were an 'iddah they would be specific to the one consummated with, and the author did not mention an 'iddah after that because it is not obligatory, because if the woman is a harbiyya there is no 'iddah upon her, and if she is a Muslim, likewise according to Abu Hanifa contrary to his two companions as will come in Al-Muhajira. Thus in Al-Hidayah following Al-Mabsut. Imam al-Tahawi mentioned the obligation of 'iddah upon her, and he made it absolute, and it should be taken as his preference for their view. And he indicated that separation depends on menstruation, so if the other converts before its completion, there is no separation. And he made absolute the conversion of one of them in dar al-harb, so it includes if the other is in dar al-Islam or in dar al-harb, whether the other stays or goes out to dar al-Islam. The gist is that as long as they have not gathered in dar al-Islam, Islam is not presented to the one who is stubborn, whether the Muslim leaves or the other, because one does not judge for an absentee nor against an absentee. Thus in Al-Muhit. And he indicated by menstruation that she is among those who menstruate; if she does not menstruate due to youth or old age, she does not become separated except after three months. And from this it is known that the case of one of the spouses converting to Islam has thirty-two aspects because the eight preceding [cases] are multiplied by four, because either they are both in dar al-Islam, or both in dar al-harb, or one in dar al-Islam only, which is true in two forms. And he did not clarify the nature of the separation, whether it is talaq or faskh due to disagreement. In Al-Siyar it is talaq according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because the expiration of this period is made a substitute for the judge's ruling, and the substitute stands in place of the original. According to Abu Yusuf it is faskh, and it is a narration from them because this separation occurred as a legal ruling, not by the judge's separation, so it is faskh, like the apostasy of the husband and his ownership of his wife. Thus in Al-Muhit. And it should be said: If the one who converted is the woman, then the separation is by talaq because the one who refuses is the husband legally, and the passage of time has been established in place of his refusal and the judge's separation, and his refusal is talaq according to them, so likewise what stands in its place. And if the one who converted is the husband, then it is faskh as mentioned earlier in her refusal, so likewise the ruling of what stands in its place. As for the occurrence of talaq upon her, if it was before the separation, there is no issue in its occurrence because she is a wife; if it was after the separation by the passage of the period, then if it is during the 'iddah according to those who make it obligatory, it occurs, otherwise not. And according to those who do not make it obligatory, she is a complete stranger, so nothing occurs. There is no doubt that these are instances of the preceding case, so they include six categories. As for the other two categories, they are excluded by his saying: 'And if the husband of a Kitābiyya converts to Islam, their marriage remains' — so it is a specification for each of the two cases, true in two forms: when the husband is Kitābi or Majūsī because the marriage is valid initially, so its continuation is more appropriate; and if she becomes Majūsī, they are separated due to the invalidity of the marriage.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the separation of spouses when one converts to Islam in dar al-harb, combined with a ruling on the waiting period. The author explains that separation does not occur immediately upon conversion; rather, a waiting period of three menses (or three months for non-menstruating women) must pass. This waiting period is not an 'iddah in the full sense, as it applies even without consummation. The Hanafi school differs on whether this separation is a talaq or a faskh. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it a talaq because the passage of time replaces the judge's decree and the husband's refusal. Abu Yusuf considers it a faskh because it occurs without a judge's ruling, similar to apostasy. The author then provides a detailed categorization of cases based on who converted and where they are located, highlighting that the ruling is complex with many scenarios. The passage also clarifies that the separation does not occur if the other spouse converts before the waiting period ends. This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah as recorded in Al-Mabsut and Al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
بينونة (baynūna): Separation between spouses; here it means the dissolution of marriage that occurs after the waiting period.
عدة ('idda): The prescribed waiting period after divorce or death; here the three menses are not considered 'idda for the Muslim woman according to Abu Hanifa, only a condition for separation.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract; it does not count as a divorce and does not allow for remarriage without a new contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In dar al-harb, if a wife converts to Islam and her husband does not, after what period does separation occur if she is of menstruating age?
A) Immediately upon conversion
B) After one menstrual cycle
C) After three menstrual cycles
D) After three months

Key Takeaway
Conversion of one spouse in dar al-harb leads to separation after three menses (or three months), classified as talaq in the mufta bihi position, not faskh.

Nikah — Marriage

The Cause of Separation: Refusal of Islam vs. Separation of Abodes
Resolves a dispute with Shafi'i over whether the cause of separation is refusal to accept Islam or separation of abodes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the cause of separation is refusal of Islam and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Separation of abodes alone does not dissolve marriage; the refusal to accept Islam is the true cause.

The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools disagree on what legally causes the dissolution of marriage when spouses reside in different abodes (dar al-Islam and dar al-harb). This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi position that the operative cause is the refusal of Islam, not mere geographical separation. Understanding this dispute requires careful analysis of the proofs and the underlying legal principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the cause of separation is the refusal of the non-Muslim spouse to accept Islam after being given the option, combined with the passage of the waiting period (menses or months).
This is based on the principle that marriage persists across abodes, as seen with musta'min.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that mere separation of abodes (tabayun al-darayn) directly causes divorce because it severs all legal connection.
Shafi'i considers the change of jurisdiction as sufficient grounds for dissolution.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i's proof is that when spouses are in different abodes, the legal connection is broken, so the marriage cannot continue.
This is a direct consequence of ihtilaf al-darayn in Shafi'i usul.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses qiyas: separation of abodes only severs guardianship, not marriage itself, as exemplified by the harbi musta'min whose marriage remains valid. Captivity (sabi) terminates marriage due to full ownership, but that is a different case.
The Hanafi school insists that the true cause is the refusal of Islam, not the abode difference.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: According to Hanafi, if both spouses are in dar al-harb and one converts, the marriage does not dissolve until the other refuses Islam after the waiting period. According to Shafi'i, the marriage dissolves immediately upon one spouse leaving dar al-Islam.
This affects rulings on subsequent marriages, inheritance, and iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتباين الدارين سبب الفرقة لا السبي والشافعي يعكسه لأن التباين أثره في انقطاع الولاية وذلك لا يؤثر في الفرقة كالحربي المستأمن والمسلم المستأمن، أما السبي فيقتضي الصفاء للسابي ولا يتحقق إلا بانقطاع النكاح ولهذا يسقط الدين عن ذمة المسبي: ولنا أن التباين حقيقة وحكماً لا ينتظم المصالح فشابه المحرمية، والسبي يوجب لا ملك الرقبة وهو مع السبب إنما هو الإباء عن الإسلام بشرط مضي الحيض أو الأشهر فيمن لا تحيض قوله (حقيقة وحكماً) قال في النهر : المراد بالتباين حقيقة تباعدهما شخصاً، وبالحكم أن لا يكون في الدار التي دخلها على سبيل الرجوع بل على سبيل القرار والسكنى حتى لو دخل الحربي دارنا بأمان لم تبن زوجته
His saying: 'And separation of abodes is the cause of separation, not captivity, and al-Shafi'i reverses it because the effect of separation of abodes is in the severance of guardianship, and that does not affect separation, like the harbi musta'min and the Muslim musta'min. As for captivity, it necessitates purity for the captor and is not realized except by the termination of marriage, and for this reason debt is dropped from the liability of the captive. For us: that separation of abodes, in reality and by legal ruling, does not organize interests, so it resembles a state of hormonal sanctity. And captivity necessitates ownership of the slave, and it is with the cause, which is only refusal of Islam with the condition of the passage of menses or months for one who does not menstruate.' His saying: 'in reality and by legal ruling.' In Al-Nahr: the meaning of separation in reality is their physical separation, and by legal ruling is that he is not in the abode he entered with the intention of returning, but with the intention of settling and residing, so that if a harbi enters our abode with aman, his wife does not become separated.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author presents the Hanafi position that the cause of separation between spouses when one converts is the refusal to accept Islam (al-iba' 'an al-Islam) conditioned on the waiting period, not the mere separation of abodes (tabayun al-darayn). The Shafi'i school holds the opposite, that separation of abodes itself causes the divorce. The Hanafi proof is that separation of abodes only severs guardianship, not marriage, as seen when a harbi enters dar al-Islam with aman and his wife remains married. Captivity (sabi) terminates marriage because it involves full ownership. The Hanafi school insists that the actual cause is the refusal to accept Islam, and the waiting period (menses or months) is the condition for separation. The commentary in Al-Nahr clarifies that 'reality and legal ruling' refers to physical distance and the intention not to return. This dispute has practical consequences: according to Shafi'i, if spouses are in different dar, marriage dissolves immediately; according to Hanafi, it only dissolves if one refuses Islam after the waiting period.

Key Terms
تباين الدارين (tabāyun al-dārayn): The condition where spouses reside in different abodes (dar al-Islam vs dar al-harb) such that legal jurisdiction differs.
إباء عن الإسلام (ibā' 'an al-Islām): Refusal to accept Islam when presented with the option, which triggers the separation after the waiting period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the actual cause (sabab) of separation when one spouse converts to Islam in dar al-harb?
A) The mere geographical separation of abodes (tabayun al-darayn)
B) The captivity (sabi) of one spouse
C) The refusal of the other spouse to accept Islam after being given the option
D) The conversion itself without any waiting period

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that the refusal to accept Islam after a waiting period is the operative cause of separation, not mere geographical separation.

Iddah for the Emigrant Woman: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the internal Hanafi dispute on iddah for an emigrant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on iddah for a non-pregnant emigrant woman, identify the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and explain the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
No iddah for the emigrant woman, because the harbi husband’s rights are not recognized in dar al-Islam.

This lesson explores the internal Hanafi dispute over whether an emigrant woman (muhajira) who leaves dar al-harb and enters dar al-Islam must observe a waiting period (iddah) before remarrying. The disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, turns on the legal effect of the separation of abodes (tabayun al-dar) and the authority of the Quranic verse 'Do not hold to the marriage bonds of disbelieving women' (60:10). Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence with rational principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the core issue? Whether an emigrant woman who is not pregnant must observe iddah before remarrying.
2
State the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa: no iddah; Sahibayn: iddah required.
The Sahibayn are Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
3
Analyze the proofs of each side
What textual and rational evidence does each side present? Abu Hanifa cites Quran 60:10 and the principle that a harbi husband has no legal standing; Sahibayn argue that separation occurred in dar al-Islam, so Islamic rulings apply.
4
Examine a subsidiary dispute on divorce during iddah
If iddah were required, what happens if the husband divorces her during that period? Abu Yusuf says the divorce does not take effect; Muhammad says it does.
This shows the practical extension of the ikhtilaf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
Which view is relied upon in the school and why? The majority of later scholars, including the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq, prefer Abu Hanifa's view.
The mufta bihi is no iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفرقة لا السبي وتنكح المهاجرة الحائل بلا عدة وارتداد أحدهما فسخ في الحال ينافي النكاح ابتداء فكذلك بقاء وصار كالشراء، ثم هو يقتضي الصفاء في محل عمله وهو المال لا في محل النكاح وفي المستأمن لم تتباين الدار حكماً لقصد الرجوع فيتفرع أربع صور: وفاقيتان وهما لو خرج الزوجان إلينا معاً ذميين أو مسلمين أو مستأمنين ثم أسلما أو صارا ذميين لا تقع الفرقة اتفاقاً، وما لو سبي أحدهما تقع الفرقة اتفاقاً عنده للسبي، وعندنا للتباين. وخلافيتان إحداهما ما إذا خرج أحدهما إلينا مسلماً أو ذمياً أو مستأمناً ثم صار بأحد الوصفين عندنا تقع فإن كان الرجل حل له التزوج بأربع في الحال وبأخت امرأته التي في دار الحرب إذا كانت في دار الإسلام وعنده لا تقع الفرقة بينه وبين زوجته التي في دار الحرب. والثانية ما إذا سبي الزوجان معاً فعنده تقع فللسابي أن يطأها بعد الاستبراء، وعندنا لا لعدم تباين داريهما أطلق في التباين فانصرف إليه حقيقة وحكماً، فلو تزوج مسلم كتابية حربية في دار الحرب فخرج عنها الزوج بانت لوجوده، ولو خرجت المرأة قبل الزوج لم تبن لأن التباين وإن وجد حقيقة لم يوجد حكماً لأنها صارت من أهل دار الإسلام لأنها التزمت أحكام المسلمين فالظاهر أنها لا تعود إلى دار الحرب والزوج من أهل دار الإسلام حكماً بخلاف ما إذا أخرجها كرهاً فإنها تبين لأنه ملكها لتحقق التباين حقيقة وحكماً لأنها في دار الحرب حكماً وزوجها في دار الإسلام حكماً، وإذا دخل الحربي دارنا بأمان لم تبن زوجته لأنه في دار الحرب حكماً فإن قبل الذمة بانت لأنه صار من أهل دارنا حقيقة وحكماً قوله : (وتنكح المهاجرة الحائل بلا عدة أي التي ليست بحامل وهذا بيان لحكم آخر جزئي من جزئیات موضوع المسألة السابقة، فإن منها ما إذا خرجت المرأة مسلمة أو ذمية وتركت زوجها في دار الحرب فأفاد أنها إذا بانت فلا عدة عليها إن لم تكن حاملاً فتتزوج للحال عند الإمام لأنه في داره حكماً إلا إذا قبل الذمة هـ. قوله : (بأحد الوصفين أي أسلم أو صار ذمياً) قوله : (فلو تزوج مسلم كتابية تفريع على أن المراد بالتباين التباين حقيقة وحكماً وهو ظاهر على ما مر من تفسيرهما. وفي الفتح عن المحيط مسلم تزوج حربية في دار الحرب فخرج بها رجل إلى دار الإسلام بانت من زوجها بالتباين فلو خرجت بنفسها قبل زوجها لم تبن لأنها صارت من أهل دارنا بالتزامها أحكام المسلمين إذ لا تمكن من العود والزوج من أهل دار الإسلام فلا تباين هـ. ووجهه في الفتح بأن المراد في الصورة الأولى إذا أخرجها الرجل قهراً حتى ملكها لتحقق التباين بينها وبين زوجها حينئذ حقيقة وحكماً أما حقيقية فظاهر وأما حكماً فلأنها في دار الحرب حكماً وزوجها في دار حكماً. قال في النهر عن الحواشي السعدية : وفي قوله وأما حكماً الخ بحث هـ. مر من معنى الحكم أن لا يكون في الدار التي دخلها على سبيل الرجوع بل على سيل الإسلام وجهه ما ولعل القرار وهي هنا كذلك إذ لا تمكن من الرجوع قال : ثم راجعت المحيط الرضوي فإذا والذي فيه ما وقالا : عليها العدة لأن الفرقة وقعت بعد الدخول في دار الإسلام فيلزمها حكم الإسلام. ولأبي حنيفة أنها أثر النكاح المتقدم ووجبت إظهاراً لحظره ولا حظر لملك الحربي ولهذا لا تتجب على المسبية، وقد تأيد ذلك بقوله تعالى ولا تمسكوا بعصم الكوافر [الممتحنة: ١٠] والعصم جمع عصمة بمعنى المنع والكوافر جمع كافرة ثم اختلفا لو خرج زوجها بعدها وهي بعد في هذه العدة فطلقها بأهل يلحقها طلاق؟ قال أبو يوسف : لا يقع عليها. وقال محمد: يقع والأصل أن الفرقة إذا وقعت بالتنافي لا تصير المرأة محلاً للطلاق عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد تصير وهو أوجه إلا أن تكون محرمة لعدم فائدة الطلاق على ما بيناه، وثمرته تظهر فيما لو طلقها ثلاثاً لا يحتاج زوجها في تزوجها إذا أسلم إلى زوج آخر عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد يحتاج إليه. كذا في فتح القدير وأراد بالمهاجرة التاركة لدار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام على عزم عدم العود وذلك بأن تخرج مسلمة أو ذمية أو صارت كذلك. وقيد بالحائل لأن الحامل لا يصح العقد عليها حتى تضع حملها، وظاهر مفهوم الكتاب أن ذلك لأجل العدة وليس كذلك كما في غاية البيان والتبيين. وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أن العقد صحيح والوطء حرام حتى تضعه لأنه لا حرمة لماء الحربي كماء الزاني، وصحح الشارحون الأول لأن النسب ثابت فكان الرحم مشغولاً بحق الغير فكان الاحتياط في منع كالوطء بخلاف الحمل من الزنا وصحح الأقطع رواية الصحة والأكثر على الأول وهو الأظهر لأنه إذا ظهر الفراش في حق النسب يظهر في حق المنع من النكاح احتياطاً.
Separation [occurs] not due to captivity; and the emigrant woman who is not pregnant is married without waiting period; and apostasy of one of them is annulment immediately. It contradicts marriage initially, so likewise in continuance, and it became like purchase. Then it necessitates purity in its place of operation, which is wealth, not in the place of marriage. And regarding the musta'min, the two abodes do not become separate legally due to intent to return. So four scenarios branch out: two agreed upon: if both spouses come out to us together as dhimmis, Muslims, or musta'mins, then they become Muslims or dhimmis, separation does not occur by agreement; and if one of them is captured, separation occurs by agreement according to him due to captivity, and according to us due to disparity [of abodes]. And two disputed: one: if one of them comes out to us as Muslim, dhimmi, or musta'min, then becomes one of the two descriptions, according to us separation occurs; so if it is the man, it becomes permissible for him to marry four immediately and his wife's sister who is in dar al-harb if she is in dar al-Islam; and according to him separation does not occur between him and his wife who is in dar al-harb. The second: if both spouses are captured together, according to him separation occurs, so the captor may have intercourse with her after istibra'; and according to us no, because their abodes are not disparate. He [the author] used absolute disparity, so it refers to real and legal [disparity]. So if a Muslim marries a Kitabi harbiyya in dar al-harb, and the husband leaves her, she becomes separated due to its existence; and if the woman leaves before the husband, she does not become separated because disparity, even if found in reality, is not found legally because she has become among the people of dar al-Islam due to her acceptance of the rulings of Muslims, and it is apparent that she will not return to dar al-harb, and the husband is among the people of dar al-Islam legally; contrary to if he forces her out, then she becomes separated because he owns her, for the realization of real and legal disparity: because she is in dar al-harb legally and her husband is in dar al-Islam legally. And if a harbi enters our dar with aman, his wife does not become separated because he is in dar al-harb legally; if he accepts dhimma, she becomes separated because he has become among the people of our dar really and legally. His statement: 'And the emigrant woman who is not pregnant is married without waiting period' means she is not pregnant, and this is a statement of another partial ruling from the particulars of the subject of the previous issue. For from them is when a woman leaves as Muslim or dhimmi and leaves her husband in dar al-harb, so it informs that when she becomes separated, there is no waiting period upon her if she is not pregnant, so she may marry immediately according to the Imam because he is in his dar legally except if he accepts dhimma. His statement: 'with one of the two descriptions' meaning he becomes Muslim or dhimmi. His statement: 'So if a Muslim marries a Kitabi woman' is a branch on the meaning of disparity being real and legal, and it is apparent based on what passed of their interpretation. And in al-Fath from al-Muhit: a Muslim married a harbiyya in dar al-harb, and a man brought her out to dar al-Islam, she becomes separated from her husband due to disparity. So if she left by herself before her husband, she does not become separated because she has become among the people of our dar by her acceptance of the rulings of Muslims, since she cannot return, and the husband is among the people of dar al-Islam, so no disparity. And its explanation in al-Fath: the meaning in the first scenario is when the man forces her out qahr until he owns her, then disparity between her and her husband is realized at that time really and legally: as for really, it is apparent; as for legally, because she is in dar al-harb legally and her husband is in dar [al-Islam] legally. He said in al-Nahr from al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya: in his saying 'and as for legally' there is investigation. It passed from the meaning of legal that one is not in the dar he entered on the basis of returning but on the basis of settlement, and she is here likewise since she cannot return. He said: Then I consulted al-Muhit al-Radawi, and behold, what is in it is what... And they two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: upon her is the waiting period because separation occurred after entering dar al-Islam, so the ruling of Islam applies to her. And for Abu Hanifa: it is a trace of the previous marriage and was obligated to manifest its prohibition, and there is no prohibition for the property of a harbi, and therefore it is not obligated upon the captured woman. And this is supported by His statement 'And do not hold to the marriage bonds of disbelieving women' [60:10]; 'al-usam' is plural of 'isma' meaning prevention, 'al-kawafir' plural of kafira. Then they differed: if her husband leaves after her while she is still in this waiting period and divorces her with [a revocable] divorce, does the divorce take effect upon her? Abu Yusuf said: it does not occur upon her. And Muhammad said: it occurs; and the principle is that when separation occurs due to contradiction, the woman does not become a locus for divorce according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad she does, and it is more appropriate except if she is prohibited because of no benefit of divorce as we explained. And its fruit appears if he divorces her three times: her husband does not need another husband to marry her after he becomes Muslim according to Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad he needs it. End quote from Fath al-Qadir. And by 'emigrant woman' is meant the one leaving dar al-harb to dar al-Islam with the intention of not returning, whether she leaves as Muslim, dhimmi, or becomes so. And it is restricted to the non-pregnant because the pregnant woman's marriage is not valid until she delivers. And the apparent implication of the book is that this is due to the waiting period, but it is not so, as in Ghayat al-Bayan wa al-Tabyin. And al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that the contract is valid and intercourse is forbidden until she delivers because the water of a harbi has no sanctity like the water of an adulterer. And the commentators validated the first because lineage is established, so the womb was occupied with the right of another, so caution was in prohibition like intercourse, contrary to pregnancy from adultery. And al-Aqta' validated the narration of validity, but most are upon the first, and it is the more evident because if the bed is established with respect to lineage, it is established with respect to prohibition of marriage as a precaution.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether an emigrant woman (مهاجرة) who leaves dar al-harb and comes to dar al-Islam, without pregnancy, must observe a waiting period (عدة) before remarrying. The author first establishes the general principle that separation of abodes (تباين الدار) terminates the marriage, then details four scenarios. Two are agreed upon: if both spouses come out together and both become Muslims or dhimmis, no separation; if one is captured, separation occurs. Two are disputed: if only one spouse comes out and becomes Muslim or dhimmi, according to the Hanafi school separation occurs, but the opposing view (likely al-Shafi'i) disagrees; if both are captured, according to the opposing view separation occurs, but according to the Hanafis it does not because their abodes are not disparate legally. Then the author turns to the specific ruling of the matn: the emigrant woman who is not pregnant may marry immediately without iddah. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that she must observe iddah because the separation occurred in dar al-Islam, and the rulings of Islam apply. Abu Hanifa's proof includes the Quranic verse 'Do not hold to the marriage bonds of disbelieving women' (60:10), which indicates that the marriage bond with a disbelieving woman cannot be maintained; she is effectively separated, and since the separation is not by divorce but by operation of law, no iddah is required. Moreover, the purpose of iddah is to show respect for the marriage and to avoid confusion of lineage, but the harbi husband's rights are not respected in dar al-Islam. The text also discusses a subsidiary issue: if the husband later divorces her during the iddah (according to the companions' view), Abu Yusuf says the divorce does not take effect because she is not a locus for divorce, while Muhammad says it does. The practical consequence is that if three divorces are issued, Abu Yusuf's position would allow remarriage without an intervening husband, while Muhammad's requires one. The author concludes that the relied-upon position (al-mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's: no iddah. The passage also addresses the case of a pregnant emigrant woman: marriage to her is not valid until she delivers, due to the need to avoid confusion of lineage.

Key Terms
مهاجرة (muhājira): A woman who abandons dar al-harb and enters dar al-Islam with the intention of permanent settlement.
حائل (hā’il): A woman who is not pregnant.
عدة (‘idda): The waiting period a woman must observe after separation from her husband before remarrying; here it is the subject of dispute.
تباين الدار (tabāyun al-dār): The legal concept of separation of abodes between dar al-Islam and dar al-harb, which can cause automatic annulment of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does an emigrant woman who is not pregnant not have to observe iddah?
A) Because she never had a valid marriage in dar al-harb
B) Because the waiting period is to respect the marriage bond, and the harbi husband's rights are not respected in dar al-Islam
C) Because she is legally considered divorced by her husband
D) Because iddah is only required for divorce, not for separation due to abode

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that an emigrant woman who is not pregnant may remarry immediately without a waiting period, based on the Quranic verse and the principle that the harbi husband's rights are not protected in dar al-Islam.

The Iddah of a Woman Emigrating from Dar al-Harb: Hanafi Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on iddah and subsequent talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the iddah of a muhajirah and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf of the intra-Hanafi dispute on talaq effectiveness.

Core Idea
A woman fleeing a harbi husband need not observe iddah according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn disagree.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school itself on the iddah of a woman who leaves Dar al-Harb. The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples illustrates how different principles—sanctity of property vs. location of separation—lead to divergent rulings. The passage also explores a secondary dispute on whether a subsequent divorce by the husband is effective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Disputes
The passage contains two distinct disputes: first, whether a muhajirah must observe iddah; second, if she observes it, whether a talaq by the husband during this iddah is valid.
The first is between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn; the second is between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
2
Analyze the First Dispute: Iddah of Muhajirah
Recognize that Abu Hanifa holds no iddah, citing Quran 60:10 and analogy to a captive woman (sabiyyah). The Sahibayn hold iddah is required because the separation occurred in Dar al-Islam after consummation.
Key proof: 'Do not hold onto the ties of disbelieving women' (60:10).
3
Examine the Proofs
For Abu Hanifa, the verse implies immediate dissolution; for the Sahibayn, the general rule of iddah applies. The text supports Abu Hanifa with a dalil but does not declare tarjih.
The secondary dispute assumes the Sahibayn's view for discussion.
4
Analyze the Second Dispute: Effectiveness of Talaq
Abu Yusuf says talaq is ineffective because the woman is no longer a valid subject due to separation; Muhammad says it is effective unless she is already prohibited (e.g., after three divorces). The text favors Muhammad's view as 'awjah'.
The thamarah: if three divorces occur, according to Muhammad a middleman is needed for remarriage.
5
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Consider a real scenario: a woman emigrates, her husband later converts and divorces her thrice. According to Abu Yusuf, they can remarry without tahlil; according to Muhammad, they need a middleman.
The mufta bihi appears to be Muhammad's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالا : عليها العدة لأن الفرقة وقعت بعد الدخول في دار الإسلام فيلزمها حكم الإسلام. ولأبي حنيفة أنها أثر النكاح المتقدم ووجبت إظهاراً لحظره ولا حظر لملك الحربي ولهذا لا تجب على المسبية، وقد تأيد ذلك بقوله تعالى ولا تمسكوا بعصم الكوافر [الممتحنة: ١٠] والعصم جمع عصمة بمعنى المنع والكوافر جمع كافرة ثم اختلفا لو خرج زوجها بعدها وهي بعد في هذه العدة فطلقها بأهل يلحقها طلاق؟ قال أبو يوسف : لا يقع عليها. وقال محمد: يقع والأصل أن الفرقة إذا وقعت بالتنافي لا تصير المرأة محلاً للطلاق عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد تصير وهو أوجه إلا أن تكون محرمة لعدم فائدة الطلاق على ما بيناه، وثمرته تظهر فيما لو طلقها ثلاثاً لا يحتاج زوجها في تزوجها إذا أسلم إلى زوج آخر عند أبي يوسف، وعند محمد يحتاج إليه. كذا في فتح القدير وأراد بالمهاجرة التاركة لدار الحرب إلى دار الإسلام على عزم عدم العود وذلك بأن تخرج مسلمة أو ذمية أو صارت كذلك.
And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Upon her is the iddah because the separation occurred after consummation in the Abode of Islam, so the ruling of Islam applies to her. And for Abu Hanifa: that (iddah) is an effect of the previous marriage, and it was required to demonstrate its prohibition, and there is no prohibition for the property of a harbi, and for this reason it is not obligatory upon a captive woman. And this is supported by the verse: 'And do not hold onto the ties of disbelieving women' (60:10), and 'isam' plural of 'isma' meaning prevention, and 'kawaafir' plural of 'kafira'. Then they differed: if her husband later comes out after that and she is still in this iddah, and he divorces her with a proper divorce, does the divorce take effect? Abu Yusuf said: It does not take place upon her. Muhammad said: It does take place. The principle is that when the separation occurs due to incompatibility, the woman does not become a valid subject for divorce according to Abu Yusuf, while according to Muhammad she does, and it is more appropriate unless she is prohibited because there is no benefit of divorce as we explained. And the practical consequence appears in that if he divorces her three times, according to Abu Yusuf her husband does not need another husband to marry her if he becomes Muslim, while according to Muhammad he does need. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And by 'muhajira' is meant the one leaving the Abode of War for the Abode of Islam with the intention of not returning, whether she leaves as a Muslim, a dhimmi, or becomes such.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the iddah of a woman who emigrates from Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam, abandoning her non-Muslim husband. The commentator begins by stating the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the woman must observe iddah because the marriage was consummated and the separation occurred in Dar al-Islam, so Islamic law applies. Abu Hanifa disagrees, arguing that iddah is a consequence of marriage and its purpose is to demonstrate the prohibition of intercourse with the wife; however, there is no such prohibition for a harbi husband, as his property (including his wife) has no sanctity in Islamic law. This is why a captive woman (sabiyyah) does not observe iddah. Abu Hanifa supports his view with the Quranic verse 'Do not hold onto the ties of disbelieving women,' indicating that the marriage bond is to be severed immediately. The commentary then examines a secondary issue: if the husband later comes to Dar al-Islam and divorces his wife while she is observing iddah (according to the Sahibayn's view), is the divorce effective? Abu Yusuf says no, because the separation due to incompatibility (tanafi) prevents the woman from being a valid subject for divorce. Muhammad says yes, the divorce is effective, and this is considered the stronger view (awjah). The practical difference arises if the husband divorces her three times: according to Abu Yusuf, if they both later become Muslim, they can remarry without the need for a middleman (tahlil), while according to Muhammad, they would need a middleman. The passage concludes by clarifying that 'muhajira' means a woman who leaves Dar al-Harb with the intention of not returning, whether she was Muslim, dhimmi, or becomes so.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after the end of a marriage to determine paternity and show mourning.
مهاجرة (muhajirah): A woman who leaves Dar al-Harb to Dar al-Islam with the intention of not returning.
عصم (isam): Plural of 'isma', meaning the marriage bond or tie that prevents separation.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under the protection of an Islamic state (as opposed to dhimmi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah) of the intra-Hanafi dispute on the effectiveness of talaq during the iddah of a muhajirah?
A) Whether the woman can remarry immediately.
B) Whether a triple talaq requires a middleman for remarriage.
C) Whether the iddah period is three months or four months.
D) Whether the woman must inform the husband of her emigration.

Key Takeaway
A woman emigrating from Dar al-Harb need not observe iddah according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn require it; if iddah is observed, a subsequent talaq is effective according to the preferred view (Muhammad).
